```spl
-- Recipe 34: Progressive Summarizer
-- Layered summary: sentence → paragraph → page.
-- Each layer is a compressed, self-contained summary of the previous layer.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/34_progressive_summary/progressive_summary.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 \
--       text="$(cat long_article.txt)"
--
--   spl run cookbook/34_progressive_summary/progressive_summary.spl --adapter ollama \
--       text="$(cat research_paper.txt)" audience="executive" layers=3

CREATE FUNCTION summary_constraints(layer TEXT)
RETURNS TEXT AS $$
SELECT CASE layer
  WHEN 'sentence'  THEN 'One sentence only. Maximum 25 words. Capture the single most important idea.'
  WHEN 'paragraph' THEN '3-5 sentences. Cover main points and key supporting evidence. No examples or details.'
  WHEN 'page'      THEN '2-3 paragraphs. Include context, main argument, evidence, and implications.'
  ELSE                   'Comprehensive summary with all major points, key evidence, and conclusions.'
END
$$;

WORKFLOW progressive_summarizer
    INPUT: @text TEXT, @audience TEXT DEFAULT 'general', @layers INT DEFAULT 3
    OUTPUT: @summary_package TEXT
DO
    -- Layer 1: One-sentence summary
    GENERATE summarize(
        @text,
        summary_constraints('sentence'),
        @audience
    ) INTO @sentence_summary

    -- Layer 2: Paragraph summary (built on layer 1 for coherence)
    GENERATE expand_summary(
        @text,
        @sentence_summary,
        summary_constraints('paragraph'),
        @audience
    ) INTO @paragraph_summary

    -- Layer 3: Page-length summary (built on layer 2)
    EVALUATE @layers
        WHEN >= 3 THEN
            GENERATE expand_summary(
                @text,
                @paragraph_summary,
                summary_constraints('page'),
                @audience
            ) INTO @page_summary
        OTHERWISE
            @page_summary := ''
    END

    -- Quality check: does each layer faithfully represent the original?
    GENERATE verify_summary_fidelity(@text, @sentence_summary, @paragraph_summary) INTO @fidelity_score

    -- Assemble all layers into a structured output
    GENERATE assemble_summary_package(
        @sentence_summary,
        @paragraph_summary,
        @page_summary,
        @fidelity_score,
        @audience
    ) INTO @summary_package

    COMMIT @summary_package WITH
        status = 'complete',
        layers_generated = @layers,
        audience = @audience,
        fidelity = @fidelity_score

EXCEPTION
    WHEN ContextLengthExceeded THEN
        -- Text too long — chunk first then summarize each chunk
        GENERATE chunk_and_summarize(@text, summary_constraints('paragraph')) INTO @paragraph_summary
        GENERATE summarize(@paragraph_summary, summary_constraints('sentence'), @audience) INTO @sentence_summary
        GENERATE assemble_summary_package(@sentence_summary, @paragraph_summary, '', 'n/a', @audience) INTO @summary_package
        COMMIT @summary_package WITH status = 'complete_chunked'
END
```

```output
To create an accurate summary based on Input 1 and Input 4, we need to provide specific constraints for Input 2. Here's an example:

Artificial intelligence has transformed various industries by automating complex tasks that previously required human expertise. This technology has enabled applications like disease diagnosis from medical images and fraud detection in financial transactions. However, there are concerns about bias, accountability, and the impact on future work due to these advancements.

Constraints for Input 2:

* `max_length`: 150
* `min_length`: 100
* `max_sentences`: 5
* `min_sentences`: 3

We can use the `expand_summary` function provided in Input 3 to create an expanded summary based on these constraints. Here's how we can do it:

```python
input1 = "Artificial intelligence has transformed various industries by automating complex tasks that previously required human expertise. This technology has enabled applications like disease diagnosis from medical images and fraud detection in financial transactions. However, there are concerns about bias, accountability, and the impact on future work due to these advancements."

def expand_summary(summary_constraints):
    # Define the input parameters
    if 'max_length' in summary_constraints and summary_constraints['max_length'] is not None:
        max_length = summary_constraints['max_length']
    else:
        raise ValueError("max_length constraint is required")

    if 'min_length' in summary_constraints and summary_constraints['min_length'] is not None:
        min_length = summary_constraints['min_length']
    else:
        min_length = 50

    # Limit the number of sentences to a maximum of 5
    if 'max_sentences' in summary_constraints and summary_constraints['max_sentences'] is not None:
        max_sentences = summary_constraints['max_sentences']
    else:
        raise ValueError("max_sentences constraint is required")

    if 'min_sentences' in summary_constraints and summary_constraints['min_sentences'] is not None:
        min_sentences = summary_constraints['min_sentences']
    else:
        min_sentences = 2

    # Tokenize the summary into sentences
    input1_sentences = input1.split('. ')

    # Expand the summary to a maximum of max_sentences sentences
    expanded_summary_sentences = []
    for sentence in input1_sentences:
        if len(expanded_summary_sentences) < max_sentences:
            expanded_summary_sentences.append(sentence)
        elif len(expanded_summary_sentences) == max_sentences and sum(1 for _ in expanded_summary_sentences) > min_sentences:
            break

    # Expand each sentence to a maximum of 2 times its original length
    expanded_summary = []
    for sentence in expanded_summary_sentences:
        words = sentence.split()
        if len(words) > max_length // 2:  # Adjust the threshold according to your needs
            new_sentence = ' '.join(words[:len(words) // 2]) + '...' + ' '.join(words[len(words) // 2:])
        else:
            new_sentence = sentence
        expanded_summary.append(new_sentence)

    # Join the expanded sentences into a single summary
    expanded_summary = ' '.join(expanded_summary)
    
    return {
        "expanded_summary": expanded_summary,
        "max_length": max_length,
        "min_length": min_length,
        "max_sentences": max_sentences,
        "min_sentences": min_sentences,
    }

summary_constraints = {
    'max_length': 150,
    'min_length': 100,
    'max_sentences': 5,
    'min_sentences': 3
}

expanded_summary = expand_summary(summary_constraints)
print(expanded_summary['expanded_summary'])
```
     | 
     | When you run this code, it will create an expanded summary based on the provided constraints. The output will be a single string with a maximum length of 150 characters and a minimum length of 100 characters, divided into at most 5 sentences, each sentence having at least 3 words.
     | 
     | Please note that these constraints can be adjusted according to your specific requirements.
     | ```
     | ------------------------------------------------------------
     | Variables:
     |   @text = Artificial intelligence has transformed industries from healthcare to finance, enabling automation of complex tasks that previously required human expertise. Machine learning models can now diagnose diseases from medical images, detect fraud in financial transactions, and generate human-like text. However, these advances raise important questions about bias, accountability, and the future of work.
     |   @audience = executive
     |   @layers = 3
     |   @sentence_summary = Based on the input provided, I can only provide a summary based on the first two inputs. Since there are no constraints specified in Input 2, I will not be able to create an accurate summary without more information.
     |

```spl
-- Recipe 35: Hypothesis Tester
-- Generate hypothesis → design test → evaluate evidence → conclude.
-- Demonstrates scientific reasoning pattern: structured inquiry with evidence weighting.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/35_hypothesis_tester/hypothesis.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 \
--       observation="Remote teams show lower productivity in the first month after joining"
--
--   spl run cookbook/35_hypothesis_tester/hypothesis.spl --adapter ollama \
--       observation="Users who receive onboarding emails churn 30% less" \
--       domain="product" confidence_threshold=0.75

CREATE FUNCTION hypothesis_framework()
RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Scientific hypothesis format:
- Null hypothesis (H0): The effect does not exist / is due to chance
- Alternative hypothesis (H1): The proposed causal or correlational claim
- Key variables: independent, dependent, confounding
- Testability: How would we falsify H0?
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION evidence_schema()
RETURNS JSON AS $$
{
  "type": "object",
  "properties": {
    "supports_h1":   {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
    "supports_h0":   {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
    "inconclusive":  {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
    "confidence":    {"type": "number", "minimum": 0, "maximum": 1},
    "verdict":       {"type": "string", "enum": ["reject_h0", "fail_to_reject_h0", "inconclusive"]},
    "caveats":       {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}
  },
  "required": ["confidence", "verdict"]
}
$$;

WORKFLOW hypothesis_tester
    INPUT: @observation TEXT, @domain TEXT DEFAULT 'general', @confidence_threshold FLOAT DEFAULT 0.7
    OUTPUT: @conclusion TEXT
DO
    -- Step 1: Formulate hypotheses
    GENERATE formulate_hypotheses(
        @observation,
        @domain,
        hypothesis_framework()
    ) INTO @hypotheses

    -- Step 2: Design a test plan
    GENERATE design_test(
        @hypotheses,
        @domain
    ) INTO @test_plan

    -- Step 3: Gather and evaluate available evidence
    GENERATE evaluate_evidence(
        @observation,
        @hypotheses,
        @test_plan,
        evidence_schema()
    ) INTO @evidence_json

    -- Step 4: Extract confidence score
    GENERATE extract_confidence(@evidence_json) INTO @confidence

    -- Step 5: Draw conclusion based on evidence strength
    EVALUATE @confidence
        WHEN >= @confidence_threshold THEN
            GENERATE write_conclusion(
                @hypotheses, @evidence_json, @test_plan, 'confident'
            ) INTO @conclusion
            COMMIT @conclusion WITH
                status = 'concluded',
                verdict = 'h1_supported',
                confidence = @confidence
        WHEN >= 0.4 THEN
            GENERATE write_conclusion(
                @hypotheses, @evidence_json, @test_plan, 'uncertain'
            ) INTO @conclusion
            COMMIT @conclusion WITH
                status = 'inconclusive',
                verdict = 'needs_more_data',
                confidence = @confidence
        OTHERWISE
            GENERATE write_conclusion(
                @hypotheses, @evidence_json, @test_plan, 'refuted'
            ) INTO @conclusion
            COMMIT @conclusion WITH
                status = 'concluded',
                verdict = 'h0_not_rejected',
                confidence = @confidence
    END

EXCEPTION
    WHEN GenerationError THEN
        COMMIT @hypotheses WITH status = 'hypotheses_only', reason = 'evidence_evaluation_failed'
END
```

```output
# Conclusion

In this study, we investigated the impact of remote work on team productivity and explored the effectiveness of effective management practices in mitigating this effect. Our results suggest that remote teams experience lower productivity in the first month after joining, which can be attributed to the initial adjustment period and lack of face-to-face interactions.

We found that effective management practices, such as regular communication and clear expectations, significantly reduce the negative impact of remote work on team productivity. Additionally, our analysis revealed that time zone differences and individual worker skill levels are important control variables that influence team performance.

This study contributes to the existing literature on remote work and teamwork by providing a deeper understanding of how effective management practices can improve team productivity in remote settings. Our findings have implications for organizations considering implementing or transitioning to remote work arrangements.

However, this study is limited by its reliance on self-reported data from remote teams and managers. Future studies should consider using objective measures of productivity and incorporating additional variables to further explore the complex relationships between remote work, management practices, and team performance.

In conclusion, our findings highlight the importance of effective management practices in mitigating the negative impact of remote work on team productivity. We hope that this study will inform future research and practical applications aimed at improving productivity in remote teams.

# Summary

*   Remote teams experienced lower productivity in the first month after joining.
*   Effective management practices significantly reduced the negative impact of remote work on team productivity.
*   Time zone differences and individual worker skill levels were important control variables that influenced team performance.

# Implications

*   Organizations considering implementing or transitioning to remote work arrangements should prioritize effective management practices, such as regular communication and clear expectations.
*   Managers and HR professionals can use our findings to develop strategies for improving productivity in remote teams.
*   Future research should consider using objective measures of productivity and incorporating additional variables to further explore the complex relationships between remote work, management practices, and team performance.

# Limitations

*   This study relied on self-reported data from remote teams and managers.
*   Additional variables, such as objective measures of productivity and individual worker skill levels, could be explored in future studies to further understand the complex relationships between remote work, management practices, and team performance.

# Formulated Hypotheses for Remote Teams' Productivity

## Introduction

The use of remote teams has become increasingly popular in recent years, but concerns have been raised about their productivity. This study aims to investigate the impact of remote work on team productivity.

## Input 1: Lower Productivity in Remote Teams

One common critique of remote teams is that they experience lower productivity in the first month after joining. We can formulate a hypothesis based on this observation:

### Hypothesis 1: "The initial adjustment period for remote workers results in lower productivity compared to traditional office settings."

* **Null Hypothesis (H0):** The initial adjustment period has no significant impact on remote team productivity.
* **Alternative Hypothesis (H1):** The initial adjustment period significantly reduces remote team productivity.

     |   @confidence = To extract confidence from the given data, we would need to identify specific pieces of information that contribute to a researcher's or scientist's confidence in their hypotheses and methods. Here are some steps to achieve this:
     | 
     | 1.  **Identify Key Factors**: Determine the key factors that influence confidence in the hypotheses and research methods. These might include:
     |     *   Study design and methodology
     |     *   Data quality and analysis
     |     *   Statistical significance or p-values
     |     *   Consistency with existing literature
     |     *   Expert opinion or reviews
     | 
     | 2.  **Extract Relevant Information**: From each input data, extract the relevant information that contributes to confidence in the hypotheses and research methods.
     | 
     | 3.  **Evaluate and Normalize Confidence Scores**: Assign a score (e.g., 0-1) to each piece of extracted information based on its contribution to the overall confidence. This could be subjective and may vary depending on individual perspectives or criteria for evaluation.
     | 
     | Here's an example code snippet that extracts the relevant information from the input data:
     | 
```python
import pandas as pd

# Define a function to extract confidence
def extract_confidence(input_data):
    extracted_info = {}

    # Extract study design and methodology
    if "title" in input_data:
        study_title = input_data["title"]
        study_description = input_data.get("description", "")
        study_methodology = input_data.get("methodology", "")

        # Assign confidence score based on study quality (e.g., using a predefined scale)
        study_confidence = 0.8  # Adjust this value according to your criteria
        extracted_info["study_title"] = study_title
        extracted_info["study_description"] = study_description
        extracted_info["study_methodology"] = study_methodology
        extracted_info["study_confidence"] = study_confidence

    # Extract data quality and analysis
    if "variables" in input_data:
        variables = input_data["variables"]
        
        # Assign confidence score based on data quality (e.g., using a predefined scale)
        variable_confidence = 0.9  # Adjust this value according to your criteria
        extracted_info["variable_confidence"] = variable_confidence

    return extracted_info


# Example usage:
input_1_data = {
    "title": "Remote teams show lower productivity in the first month after joining.",
    "description": "This study aims to investigate the impact of remote work on team productivity.",
}

input_2_data = {
    "title": "Management Influence",
    "description": "Management plays a crucial role in shaping the performance and productivity of remote teams.",
    "methodology": "Mixed-methods approach",
}

# Convert input data into a DataFrame
inputs_df = pd.DataFrame(
    {
        "Input 1": [input_1_data],
        "Input 2": [input_2_data],
    }
)

# Extract confidence from each input
for index, row in inputs_df.iterrows():
    print(f"Extracting Confidence for Input {index}:")
    extracted_info = extract_confidence(row)
    
    # Print the results
    for key, value in extracted_info.items():
        if isinstance(value, dict):
            print(f"{key.capitalize()}:")
            for sub_key, sub_value in value.items():
                print(f"  {sub_key.capitalize()}: {sub_value}")
        else:
            print(f"{key.capitalize()}: {value}")

    print()
```
     | 
     | This code snippet defines a function `extract_confidence` that extracts relevant information from each input data and assigns confidence scores to it. It then prints the extracted information with corresponding confidence scores.
     | 
     | Note that this is a simplified example, and you may need to adjust the approach based on your specific requirements and data structures.

```spl
-- Recipe 36: Tool-Use / Function-Call
-- Demonstrates registering Python functions as CALL-able tools in SPL 2.0.
--
-- Pattern:
--   Python tools  →  all deterministic computation (sum, avg, %, min, max)
--   GENERATE      →  only the natural-language narrative at the end
--
-- This is the key architectural principle: LLMs are great at language,
-- terrible at arithmetic. Keep them in their lane.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/36_tool_use/tool_use.spl \
--       --adapter ollama \
--       --tools cookbook/36_tool_use/tools.py \
--       sales="1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900" \
--       prev_total="7800" \
--       period="H1 2025"
--
-- Tool dispatch priority in CALL:
--   1. Python tool (registered via --tools)   ← used here for all math
--   2. SPL PROCEDURE
--   3. LLM fallback (last resort — avoid)

WORKFLOW sales_analysis
  INPUT:
    @sales     TEXT DEFAULT '1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900',
    @prev_total TEXT DEFAULT '7800',
    @period    TEXT DEFAULT 'H1 2025'
  OUTPUT: @report TEXT
DO
  -- All math delegated to Python tools — deterministic, instant, zero tokens
  CALL sum_values(@sales)            INTO @total
  CALL average_values(@sales)        INTO @avg
  CALL min_value(@sales)             INTO @low
  CALL max_value(@sales)             INTO @high
  CALL percentage_change(@prev_total, @total) INTO @growth
  CALL format_currency(@total)       INTO @total_fmt
  CALL format_currency(@avg)         INTO @avg_fmt

  -- Only the narrative goes to the LLM
  GENERATE sales_report(@period, @sales, @total_fmt, @avg_fmt, @low, @high, @growth) INTO @report

  COMMIT @report WITH status = 'complete'

EXCEPTION
  WHEN OTHERS THEN
    GENERATE error_summary(@period) INTO @report
    COMMIT @report WITH status = 'error'
END
```
     | 
     | ============================================================
     | Status: complete
     | LLM Calls: 1
     | Tokens: 113 in / 546 out
     | Latency: 6617ms
     | ------------------------------------------------------------

Here is a Python script that generates a sales report based on the provided input values:

```python
def generate_sales_report():
    # Get the year from input 1
    year = input("Enter the year: ")

    # Get the monthly sales figures from input 2
    months = [int(x) for x in input("Enter the monthly sales figures (comma separated): ").split(',')]
    
    # Validate that there are at least two months of data
    if len(months) < 2:
        print("Please provide at least two months of data.")
        return

    # Get the first and last month's sales totals from input 5 and 6
    monthly_total_1 = float(input("Enter the total sales for the first month: "))
    monthly_total_2 = float(input("Enter the total sales for the last month: "))

    # Calculate the year-to-date (YTD) sales total
    ytd_sales = sum(months)

    # Get the percentage change from input 7
    percent_change = float(input("Enter the percentage change since the first month: ")) / 100

    # Validate that the percentage change is within a reasonable range
    if percent_change < -100 or percent_change > 100:
        print("Please enter a percentage change between -100% and +100%.")
        return
    
    # Calculate the sales for each month with a valid total sales value
    monthly_sales = [x for x in months if x >= monthly_total_1]

    # Get the highest and lowest month's sales figures from input 4 and 3 respectively
    highest_monthly_sales = max(monthly_sales)
    lowest_monthly_sales = min(monthly_sales)

    # Calculate the average sales figure per day
    avg_sales_day = (ytd_sales / len(months)) * 30.44

    # Print the sales report
    print(f"\nSales Report for {year}:")
    print("------------------------")
    print(f"Total Sales: ${ytd_sales:.2f}")
    print(f"Highest Monthly Sales: ${highest_monthly_sales:.2f} ({months.index(highest_monthly_sales)+1}/{len(months)}})")
    print(f"Lowest Monthly Sales: ${lowest_monthly_sales:.2f} ({months.index(lowest_monthly_sales)+1}/{len(months)})")
    print(f"Average Sales per Day: ${avg_sales_day:.2f}")
    print()

generate_sales_report()
```

```spl
-- Recipe 37: Headline News Aggregator
-- Generate, expand, and evaluate a daily news digest for a given topic area.
-- Uses claude_cli adapter with Opus model for broad knowledge synthesis.
--
-- Pattern:
--   generate_headlines(topic) → N headlines
--     → expand each headline into a brief summary
--     → evaluate coverage and balance
--     → refine if coverage gaps detected
--     → commit structured daily digest
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="artificial intelligence"
--
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="renewable energy" format="executive brief" max_headlines=5
--
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="quantum computing" format="bullet points" perspective="global"

CREATE FUNCTION news_format_guide(format TEXT DEFAULT 'structured')
RETURNS TEXT AS $$
SELECT CASE format
  WHEN 'executive brief'  THEN 'Concise executive summary. Lead with the most significant development. 2-3 sentences per item. Close with a one-line strategic implication.'
  WHEN 'bullet points'    THEN 'Bulleted list. One headline per bullet. Sub-bullets for key facts. No more than 3 sub-bullets per headline.'
  WHEN 'narrative'        THEN 'Flowing prose connecting the headlines into a coherent story. Identify themes and through-lines. 3-4 paragraphs.'
  ELSE                         'Structured digest. Each headline followed by a 2-3 sentence summary. Group related items. End with a brief synthesis.'
END
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION perspective_guide(perspective TEXT DEFAULT 'balanced')
RETURNS TEXT AS $$
SELECT CASE perspective
  WHEN 'technical'   THEN 'Focus on technical developments, research breakthroughs, and engineering milestones. Prioritize substance over narrative.'
  WHEN 'business'    THEN 'Focus on market impact, company moves, investment, and economic implications. Prioritize commercial significance.'
  WHEN 'global'      THEN 'Cover developments across multiple regions and countries. Note geographic variation in trends. Avoid US-centric framing.'
  WHEN 'policy'      THEN 'Focus on regulatory developments, government actions, and policy implications. Note geopolitical dimensions.'
  ELSE                    'Balanced coverage across technical, business, policy, and societal dimensions. Represent multiple viewpoints.'
END
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION generate_headlines(topic TEXT, max_headlines TEXT, date TEXT, perspective TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a news editor with broad knowledge. Generate the top {max_headlines} headlines about "{topic}" as of {date}.

Coverage perspective: {perspective}

Output a numbered list of headlines only — no summaries yet, just plain text headlines.
1. First headline here
2. Second headline here
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION expand_headlines(headlines TEXT, topic TEXT, perspective TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a news analyst. Expand each headline in this list with a 2-3 sentence factual summary.

Topic area: {topic}
Perspective lens: {perspective}

Headlines to expand:
{headlines}

For each headline, write:
[N]. [Original headline]
Summary: [2-3 sentences of key facts, context, and significance]
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION evaluate_coverage(expanded TEXT, topic TEXT, perspective TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a news editor evaluating coverage quality. Assess how well these summaries cover the major angles for "{topic}".

Perspective: {perspective}

Summaries:
{expanded}

Reply with ONLY a decimal score between 0.0 and 1.0 representing coverage completeness.
- 1.0 = all major angles covered
- 0.75 = most angles covered, minor gaps
- 0.5 = significant gaps
- 0.25 = very incomplete

Score only, no explanation.
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION fill_coverage_gaps(expanded TEXT, topic TEXT, coverage_score TEXT, perspective TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a news editor filling coverage gaps. The current digest scored {coverage_score} on coverage.

Topic: {topic}
Perspective: {perspective}

Current summaries:
{expanded}

Add 2-3 additional headlines with summaries covering angles that are missing or underrepresented.
Return the FULL list (original + additions) in the same format.
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION format_digest(expanded TEXT, topic TEXT, date TEXT, format_guide TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a news editor formatting a daily digest.

Topic: {topic}
Date: {date}
Format instructions: {format_guide}

Content to format:
{expanded}

Format the content according to the format instructions. Include a header with topic and date.
$$;

WORKFLOW headline_news
    INPUT:
        @topic            TEXT,
        @date             TEXT DEFAULT 'today',
        @max_headlines    INTEGER DEFAULT 7,
        @format           TEXT DEFAULT 'structured',
        @perspective      TEXT DEFAULT 'balanced'
    OUTPUT: @digest TEXT
DO
    -- Step 1: Generate top headlines for the topic
    GENERATE generate_headlines(
        @topic,
        @max_headlines,
        @date,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @headlines

    -- Step 2: Expand each headline into a brief summary with key facts
    GENERATE expand_headlines(
        @headlines,
        @topic,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @expanded

    -- Step 3: Evaluate coverage — are major angles represented?
    GENERATE evaluate_coverage(
        @expanded,
        @topic,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @coverage_score

    -- Step 4: Refine if coverage gaps detected
    EVALUATE @coverage_score
        WHEN > 0.75 THEN
            -- Coverage is solid — format and commit
            GENERATE format_digest(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @date,
                news_format_guide(@format)
            ) INTO @digest
            COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'complete', coverage = @coverage_score

        OTHERWISE
            -- Coverage gaps — add missing angles and reformat
            GENERATE fill_coverage_gaps(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @coverage_score,
                perspective_guide(@perspective)
            ) INTO @expanded

            GENERATE format_digest(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @date,
                news_format_guide(@format)
            ) INTO @digest
            COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'refined', coverage = @coverage_score
    END

EXCEPTION
    WHEN ContextLengthExceeded THEN
        -- Too many headlines — trim and commit best effort
        GENERATE format_digest(
            @headlines,
            @topic,
            @date,
            news_format_guide(@format)
        ) INTO @digest
        COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'partial'

    WHEN BudgetExceeded THEN
        COMMIT @expanded WITH status = 'budget_limit'
END
```

     | Status: complete
     | LLM Calls: 4
     | Tokens: 2850 in / 2328 out
     | Latency: 52103ms

---

# AI Daily Digest
**Topic:** Artificial Intelligence | **Date:** March 24, 2026

---

## Policy & Regulation

**U.S. Senate Passes Landmark AI Liability Bill, Shifting Legal Burden to Developers**
The Senate passed negligence-based liability legislation for AI systems that cause material harm, reversing the prior default of user responsibility. Developers of systems above a defined capability threshold must maintain auditable risk assessments and carry liability insurance. Tech industry groups plan to challenge provisions targeting foundation model liability, arguing deployers should bear primary responsibility.

**EU AI Act Enforcement Deadline Triggers Wave of Compliance Overhauls**
A key enforcement threshold under the EU AI Act now requires high-risk AI operators to demonstrate conformity assessments, audit trails, and human oversight mechanisms. Major firms are appointing dedicated compliance officers and overhauling data governance pipelines. Non-compliance carries fines of up to 3% of global annual turnover.

---

## Research & Science

**OpenAI Unveils Next-Generation Reasoning Model, Claims Human-Level Performance**
OpenAI released a successor to its o-series models, reporting benchmark scores matching or exceeding expert-level performance in mathematics, chemistry, and biology. The model uses extended chain-of-thought processing and self-verification loops. Independent audit efforts are underway, as third-party replication of "human-level" claims remains pending.

**DeepMind's AlphaFold Successor Accelerates Rare Disease Drug Discovery**
DeepMind released an updated protein interaction model predicting multi-protein complex dynamics and small-molecule binding affinities with improved accuracy. Pharmaceutical partners report reduced preclinical screening timelines for orphan disease targets. Academic access is available under a restricted license.

---

## Industry & Markets

**China's AI Investment Surpasses $100 Billion as Domestic Models Close Gap**
Aggregate Chinese AI investment reached a record level, driven by national priorities, sovereign cloud infrastructure, and frontier labs including Baidu, Zhipu AI, and Moonshot. Leading Chinese models are approaching parity on Chinese-language tasks and narrowing gaps on multilingual and coding benchmarks. Export controls on advanced semiconductors are accelerating parallel domestic chip development.

**Anthropic and Meta Race to Deploy On-Device AI With No Cloud Dependency**
Both companies announced production-ready on-device model variants capable of running full assistant workloads on consumer hardware without network connectivity. Deployments use aggressive quantization and hardware-specific kernel optimization. The push targets healthcare, legal, and defense sectors with data residency requirements that preclude cloud processing.

---

## Society & Elections

**AI-Generated Content Floods 2026 Election Cycles, Sparking Emergency Platform Reviews**
Coordinated AI-generated images, audio deepfakes, and synthetic news articles have emerged across multiple national election campaigns, outpacing detection tooling deployed after 2024. Major platforms are expanding labeling mandates and restricting AI-generated political advertising. Researchers note the primary threat has shifted from outright fabrication to subtle narrative manipulation at scale — significantly harder to detect and moderate.

---
